	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">British Virgin Islands</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the island group, which also includes the United States Virgin Islands and Spanish Virgin Islands, see <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>.</div>

href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.vg" title=".vg">.vg</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>British Virgin Islands</b> (abbreviated <b>BVI</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> officially simply the <b>Virgin Islands</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> are a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">British Overseas Territory</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, to the east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">US Virgin Islands</a> and north-west of <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>. The islands are geographically part of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands archipelago</a> and are located in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.
</p><p>The British Virgin Islands consist of the main islands of <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda" title="Virgin Gorda">Virgin Gorda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anegada" title="Anegada">Anegada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jost_Van_Dyke" title="Jost Van Dyke">Jost Van Dyke</a>, along with over 50 other smaller islands and <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> About 16 of the islands are inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The capital, <a href="/wiki/Road_Town" title="Road Town">Road Town</a>, is on Tortola, the largest island, which is about 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) long and 5&#160;km (3&#160;mi) wide. The islands had a population of about 28,000 at the 2010 Census, of whom approximately 23,500 lived on Tortola;<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> current estimates put the population at 35,800 (July 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>British Virgin Islanders are <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_citizen" title="British Overseas Territories citizen">British Overseas Territories citizens</a> and since 2002 are <a href="/wiki/British_citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="British citizen">British citizens</a> as well. Although the territory is not part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and not directly subject to EU law, British Virgin Islanders are deemed to be citizens of the EU by virtue of their British citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The islands were named "Santa Úrsula y las Once Mil Vírgenes" by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in 1493 after the legend of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ursula" title="Saint Ursula">Saint Ursula</a> and the 11,000 virgins.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The name name was later shortened to "the Virgin Islands".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The official name of the territory is still simply the "Virgin Islands", but the prefix "British" is often used. This is commonly believed to distinguish it from the neighbouring American territory which changed its name from the "<a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a>" to "<a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Islands of the United States">Virgin Islands of the United States</a>" in 1917. However, local historians have disputed this, pointing to a variety of publications and public records dating from between 21 February 1857 and 12 September 1919 where the Territory is referred to as the <i>British</i> Virgin Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Moll_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moll-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> British Virgin Islands government publications continue to begin with the name "The territory of the Virgin Islands", and <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands_passport" class="mw-redirect" title="British Virgin Islands passport">the territory's passports</a> simply refer to the "Virgin Islands", and all laws begin with the words "Virgin Islands". Moreover, the territory's Constitutional Commission has expressed the view that "every effort should be made" to encourage the use of the name "Virgin Islands".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> But various public and quasi-public bodies continue to use the name "British Virgin Islands" or "BVI", including BVI Finance, BVI Electricity Corporation, BVI Tourist Board, BVI Athletic Association, <a href="/wiki/BVI_Bar_Association" title="BVI Bar Association">BVI Bar Association</a> and others.
</p><p>In 1968 the British Government issued a memorandum requiring that the postage stamps in the territory should say "British Virgin Islands" (whereas previously they had simply stated "Virgin Islands"), a practice which is still followed today.<sup id="cite_ref-Moll_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moll-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This was likely to prevent confusion following on from the adoption of US currency in the Territory in 1959, and the references to US currency on the stamps of the Territory.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="History of the British Virgin Islands">History of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>It is generally thought that the Virgin Islands were first settled by the <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a> from South America around 100 BC-200 AD, though there is some evidence of <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> presence on the islands as far back as 1500 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Arawaks inhabited the islands until the 15th century when they were displaced by the more aggressive <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>, a tribe from the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> islands.
</p><p>The first European sighting of the Virgin Islands was by the Spanish expedition of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in 1493 on his second voyage to the Americas, who gave the islands their modern name.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> claimed the islands by discovery in the early 16th century, but never settled them, and subsequent years saw the English, Dutch, French, Spanish, and Danish all jostling for control of the region, which became a notorious haunt for <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Piracy in the British Virgin Islands">pirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> There is no record of any native Amerindian population in the British Virgin Islands during this period; it is thought that they either fled to safer islands or were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Dutch established a <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Virgin_Islands" title="Dutch Virgin Islands">permanent settlement</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a> by 1648,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> frequently clashing with the Spanish who were based on nearby Puerto Rico. In 1672, the English captured Tortola from the Dutch, and the English annexation of <a href="/wiki/Anegada" title="Anegada">Anegada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda" title="Virgin Gorda">Virgin Gorda</a> followed in 1680.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Meanwhile, over the period 1672–1733, the Danish gained control of the nearby islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a> (i.e. the modern US Virgin Islands).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Phillips_Church,_Tortola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg/220px-St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg/330px-St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg/440px-St_Phillips_Church%2C_Tortola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Phillips_Church,_Tortola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ruins of <a href="/wiki/St._Phillip%27s_Anglican_Church_(BVI)" title="St. Phillip&#39;s Anglican Church (BVI)">St. Phillip's Church, Tortola</a>, one of the most important historical ruins in the territory.</div></div></div>
<p>The British islands were considered principally a strategic possession. The British introduced <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> which was to become the main crop and source of foreign trade, and large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Slavery in the British Virgin Islands">slaves</a> were forcibly brought from Africa to work on the sugar cane plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The islands prospered economically until the middle of the nineteenth century, when a combination of the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of slavery">abolition of slavery</a> in the British Empire in 1834, a series of disastrous hurricanes, and the growth in the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beet</a> crop in Europe and the United States<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> significantly reduced sugar cane production and led to a period of economic decline.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1917, the United States purchased the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Virgin Islands">Danish Virgin Islands</a> for US$25 million, renaming them the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>. Economic linkages with the US islands prompted the British Virgin Islands to adopt the US dollar as its currency in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The British Virgin Islands were administered variously as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a> or with <a href="/wiki/St._Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Kitts and Nevis">St. Kitts and Nevis</a>, with an administrator representing the British Government on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The islands gained separate colony status in 1960 and became autonomous in 1967 under the new post of Chief Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1960s, the islands have diversified away from their traditionally agriculture-based economy towards tourism and financial services, becoming one of the wealthiest areas in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The constitution of the islands was amended in 1977, 2004 and 2007, giving them greater local autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Irma_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Effects of Hurricane Irma in the British Virgin Islands">struck the islands</a>, causing four deaths and immense damage.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Geography of the British Virgin Islands">Geography of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GB_Virgin_Islands.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/GB_Virgin_Islands.png/500px-GB_Virgin_Islands.png" decoding="async" width="500" height="333" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/GB_Virgin_Islands.png 1.5x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GB_Virgin_Islands.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of British Virgin Islands (Note: Anegada is farther away from the other islands than shown)</div></div></div>
<p>The British Virgin Islands comprise around 60 tropical Caribbean islands, ranging in size from the largest, Tortola, being 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) long and 5&#160;km (3&#160;mi) wide, to tiny uninhabited <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>, altogether about 150 square kilometres (58 square miles) in extent. They are located in the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands archipelago</a>, a few miles east of the <a href="/wiki/US_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="US Virgin Islands">US Virgin Islands</a>, and about 95&#160;km (59&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican</a> mainland. About 150&#160;km (93&#160;mi) east south-east lies <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a> lies to the east of the islands, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> lies to the west. Most of the islands are volcanic in origin and have a hilly, rugged terrain.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Sage" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Sage">Mount Sage</a> on Tortola at 52m.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Anegada is geologically distinct from the rest of the group, being a flat island composed of limestone and coral.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A full list of the territory's islands can be found below:
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of the British Virgin Islands">Climate of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg/1000px-British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg/1500px-British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg/2000px-British_Virgin_Islands_WV_banner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="12117" data-file-height="1740" /></a></div></div></div>
<p>The British Virgin Islands have a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a>, moderated by <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Temperatures vary little throughout the year. In the capital, <a href="/wiki/Road_Town" title="Road Town">Road Town</a>, typical daily maxima are around 32&#160;°C (89.6&#160;°F) in the summer and 29&#160;°C (84.2&#160;°F) in the winter. Typical daily minima are around 24&#160;°C (75.2&#160;°F) in the summer and 21&#160;°C (69.8&#160;°F) in the winter. Rainfall averages about 1,150&#160;mm (45.3&#160;in) per year, higher in the hills and lower on the coast. Rainfall can be quite variable, but the wettest months on average are September to November and the driest months on average are February and March.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricanes">Hurricanes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hurricanes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hurricanes occasionally hit the islands, with the hurricane season running from June to November. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Danny_(2015)" title="Hurricane Danny (2015)">Hurricane Danny</a> struck in 2015.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irma">Hurricane Irma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Irma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Irma_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Effects of Hurricane Irma in the British Virgin Islands">Effects of Hurricane Irma in the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/220px-Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/330px-Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/440px-Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Main_Street_Road_Town_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Damage in Road Town following Hurricane Irma</div></div></div>
<p>The islands were struck by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> on 6 September 2017, causing extensive damage,<sup id="cite_ref-metro.co.uk_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro.co.uk-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> as well as four deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A state of emergency was declared by the Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The most significant damage was on Tortola.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The UK's then-Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> visited Tortola on 13 September 2017 and said that he was reminded of photos of Hiroshima after it had been hit by the atom bomb.<sup id="cite_ref-sky.com_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sky.com-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 8 September, the UK government sent troops with medical supplies and other aid.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> More troops were expected to arrive a day or two later, but the ship
HMS Ocean, carrying more extensive assistance, was not expected to reach the islands for another two weeks, however.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, a resident of <a href="/wiki/Necker_Island_(British_Virgin_Islands)" title="Necker Island (British Virgin Islands)">Necker Island</a>, called on the UK government to develop a massive disaster recovery plan for British islands that were damaged, to include "both through short-term aid and long-term infrastructure spending".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Premier <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Smith" title="Orlando Smith">Orlando Smith</a> also called for a comprehensive aid package to rebuild the BVI. On 10 September UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> pledged £32 million to the Caribbean for a Hurricane relief fund; the UK government would also match donations made by the public via the British Red Cross appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Specifics were not provided to the news media as to the amount that would be allocated to the Virgin Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Boris Johnson's visit to Tortola on 13 September 2017 during his Caribbean tour was intended to confirm the UK's commitment to helping restore British islands but he provided no additional comments on the aid package.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He did confirm that <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS Ocean (L12)</a> was on the way to the BVI items like timber, buckets, bottled water, food, baby milk, bedding and clothing, as well as ten pickup trucks, building materials and hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Politics of the British Virgin Islands">Politics of the British Virgin Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Elections in the British Virgin Islands">Elections in the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_LegCo_Building,_Road_Town.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg/220px-Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg/330px-Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg/440px-Old_LegCo_Building%2C_Road_Town.jpg 2x" data-file-width="884" data-file-height="657" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_LegCo_Building,_Road_Town.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Legislative Council building in <a href="/wiki/Road_Town" title="Road Town">Road Town</a>. The High Court sits upstairs.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</div></div></div>
<p>The territory operates as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Ultimate executive authority in the British Virgin Islands is vested in <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">the Queen</a>, and is exercised on her behalf by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of the British Virgin Islands">Governor of the British Virgin Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The governor is appointed by the Queen on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/British_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="British Government">British government</a>. Defence and most foreign affairs remain the responsibility of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Constitution of the British Virgin Islands">most recent constitution</a> was adopted in 2007 (the Virgin Islands Constitution Order, 2007)<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and came into force when the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Council of the British Virgin Islands">Legislative Council</a> was dissolved for the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands_general_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="British Virgin Islands general election, 2007">2007 general election</a>. The head of government under the constitution is the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of the British Virgin Islands">Premier</a> (before the new constitution the office was referred to as <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister of the British Virgin Islands">Chief Minister</a>), who is elected in a general election along with the other members of the ruling government as well as the members of the opposition. <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Elections in the British Virgin Islands">Elections</a> are held roughly every four years. A <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Cabinet of the British Virgin Islands">cabinet</a> is nominated by the Premier and appointed and chaired by the Governor. The Legislature consists of the Queen (represented by the Governor) and a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="House of Assembly of the British Virgin Islands">House of Assembly</a> made up of 13 elected members plus the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_House_of_Assembly_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="List of Speakers of the House of Assembly of the British Virgin Islands">Speaker</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Attorney General of the British Virgin Islands">Attorney General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current Governor is <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Jaspert" title="Augustus Jaspert">Augustus Jaspert</a> (since 22 August 2017).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The current Premier is <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fahie" title="Andrew Fahie">Andrew Fahie</a> (since 26 February 2019), who is leader of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Party" title="Virgin Islands Party">Virgin Islands Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Districts of the British Virgin Islands">Districts of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The British Virgin Islands is a unitary territory. The territory is divided into nine electoral districts, and each voter is registered in one of those districts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Eight of the nine districts are partly or wholly on Tortola, and encompass nearby neighbouring islands. Only the ninth district (Virgin Gorda and Anegada) does not include any part of Tortola. At elections, in addition to voting their local representative, voters also cast votes for four "at-large" candidates who are elected upon a territory-wide basis.
</p><p>The territory is also technically divided into five administrative districts (one for each of the four largest islands, with the fifth covering all other islands), and into six civil registry districts (three for Tortola, Jost Van Dyke, Virgin Gorda and Anegada) although these have little practical relevance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_criminal_justice">Law and criminal justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Law and criminal justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Law of the British Virgin Islands">Law of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>Crime in the British Virgin Islands is comparatively low by Caribbean standards (and indeed compared to the neighbouring US Virgin Islands).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  Whilst statistics and hard data are relatively rare, and are not regularly published by governmental sources in the British Virgin Islands, the Premier did announce that in 2013 there has been a 14% decline in recorded crime as against 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>  Homicides are rare,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> with just one incident recorded in 2013. 
</p><p>The British and US Virgin Islands sit at the axis of a major drugs transshipment point between Latin America and the continental United States.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The American <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a> regards the adjacent US territories of Puerto Rico and the US Virgin Islands as a "High Intensity Drug Trafficking Area".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>  A co-operation agreement exists between the British Virgin Islands and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">US Coast Guard</a> allowing American forces to pursue suspected drug traffickers through the territorial waters of the British Virgin Islands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In August 2011 a joint raid between the <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">American DEA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Virgin_Islands_Police_Force" title="Royal Virgin Islands Police Force">Royal Virgin Islands Police Force</a> arrested a number of British Virgin Islands residents who are accused of being involved in major drugs <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipments</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> although their extradition to the United States has since become stalled in protracted legal wrangling.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Military of the British Virgin Islands">Military of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>As a British Overseas territory, defence of the islands is the responsibility of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Economy of the British Virgin Islands">Economy of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roadtown,_Tortola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg/220px-Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg/330px-Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg/440px-Roadtown%2C_Tortola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roadtown,_Tortola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Road_Town" title="Road Town">Road Town</a>, Tortola, British Virgin Islands</div></div></div>
<p>The twin pillars of the economy are tourism (roughly 40-45% of GDP) and financial services (60%).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Politically, tourism is the more important of the two, as it employs a greater number of people within the territory, and a larger proportion of the businesses in the tourist industry are locally owned, as are a number of the highly tourism-dependent sole traders (for example, taxi drivers and street vendors). Economically however, financial services associated with the territory's status as an offshore financial centre are by far the more important. 51.8% of the Government's revenue comes directly from licence fees for offshore companies, and considerable further sums are raised directly or indirectly from payroll taxes relating to salaries paid within the trust industry sector (which tend to be higher on average than those paid in the tourism sector).
</p><p>The official currency of the British Virgin Islands has been the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> (US$) since 1959, the currency also used by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Deemed by some to be a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> due to its opaque banking system,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smh2013_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smh2013-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> the British Virgin Islands enjoys one of the more prosperous economies of the Caribbean region, with a per capita average income of around $42,300 (2010 est.) <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The average monthly income earned by a worker in the territory was US$2,452 as at the time of the 2010 Census.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> 29% of the population fell into the "low income" category.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Although it is common to hear criticism in the British Virgin Islands' press about <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">income inequality</a>, no serious attempt has been made by economists to calculate a <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> or similar measure of income equality for the territory.  A report from 2000 suggested that, despite the popular perception, income inequality was actually lower in the British Virgin Islands than in any other OECS state,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> although in global terms income equality is higher in the Caribbean than in many other regions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg/220px-TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg/330px-TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg/440px-TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TheBaths_VirginGorda_BVI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Baths" title="The Baths">The Baths</a>, Virgin Gorda</div></div></div>
<p>Tourism accounts for approximately 45% of national income.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The islands are a popular destination for US citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Tourists frequent the numerous white sand beaches, visit <a href="/wiki/The_Baths" title="The Baths">The Baths on Virgin Gorda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkel</a> the <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> near Anegada, or experience the well-known bars of Jost Van Dyke. The BVI are known as one of the world's greatest sailing destinations, and charter sailboats are a very popular way to visit less accessible islands. Every year since 1972 the BVI has hosted the Spring Regatta, which is a seven-day collection of sailing races throughout the islands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A substantial number of the tourists who visit the BVI are <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ship</a> passengers, and although they produce far lower revenue per head than charter boat tourists and hotel based tourists, they are nonetheless important to the substantial - and politically important - taxi driving community. Only Virgin Islanders are permitted to work as taxi drivers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Financial services account for over half of the income of the territory. The majority of this revenue is generated by the licensing of <a href="/wiki/Offshore_company" title="Offshore company">offshore companies</a> and related services. The British Virgin Islands is a significant global player in the <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial services industry</a>. In 2000 <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> reported in its survey of <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">offshore jurisdictions</a> for the United Kingdom government that over 45% of the world's offshore companies were formed in the British Virgin Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  Since 2001, financial services in the British Virgin Islands have been regulated by the independent <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands_Financial_Services_Commission" title="British Virgin Islands Financial Services Commission">Financial Services Commission</a>.
</p><p>At the end of 2012 the banking sector of the British Virgin Islands comprised six commercial banks<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and one restricted bank, 12 authorised custodians, two licensed money services businesses and one licensed financing service provider.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As such the British Virgin Islands is frequently labelled as a "<a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>" by campaigners and NGOs,<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianNov2012_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianNov2012-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and has been expressly named in anti-tax haven legislation in other countries on various occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>  Successive governments in the British Virgin Islands have fought against the tax haven label, and made various commitments to tax exchange and recording beneficial ownership information of companies following the <a href="/wiki/39th_G8_summit" title="39th G8 summit">2013 G8 summit</a>.  On 10 September 2013 British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> said "I do not think it is fair any longer to refer to any of the Overseas Territories or Crown Dependencies as tax havens.  They have taken action to make sure that they have fair and open tax systems.  It is very important that our focus should now shift to those territories and countries that really are tax havens."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the April 2016 <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a> leak, the British Virgin Islands was the most commonly used tax haven by clients of <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act">Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On June 30, 2014, The British Virgin Islands<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> was deemed to have an Inter- Governmental Agreement (IGA) with the United States of America with respect to  the "Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act" of the United States of America.
</p><p>The Model 1 Agreement (14 Pages)<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> recognizes that: <i>The Government of Great Britain and Northern Ireland provided a copy of the Letter of Entrustment which was sent to the Government of the British Virgin Islands, to the Government of the United States of America "via diplomatic note of May 28, 2014".</i>
</p><p>The Letter of Entrustment dated July 14, 2010 was originally provided to the Government of the British Virgin Islands and authorised the Government of the BVI "to negotiate and conclude Agreements relating to taxation that provide for exchange of information on tax matters to the OECD standard" (Paragraph 2 of the FATCA Agreement). Via an "Entrustment Letter" dated March 24, 2014, The Govt of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, authorized the Govt of the BVI to sign an agreement on information exchange to facilitate the Implementation of the Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On March 27, 2017, the US Treasury site disclosed that the Model 1 agreement and related agreement were "In Force" on July 13, 2015.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions_and_Anti-Money_Laundering_Act">Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Under the UK Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act of 2018, beneficial ownership of companies in British overseas territories such as the British Virgin Islands must be publicly registered for disclosure by 31 December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-kmppvap_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kmppvap-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  The Government of the British Virgin Islands plans to challenge this law, arguing that it violates the Constitutional sovereignty granted to the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-kmppvap_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kmppvap-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_industry">Agriculture and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Agriculture and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Agriculture and industry account for only a small proportion of the islands' GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Agricultural produce includes fruit, vegetables, sugar cane, livestock and poultry, and industries include rum distillation, construction and boat building. Commercial fishing is also practised in the islands' waters.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Workforce">Workforce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Workforce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The British Virgin Islands is heavily dependent on migrant workers, and over 50% of all workers on the islands are of a foreign descent. Only 37% of the entire population were born in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The national labour-force is estimated at 12,770, of whom approximately 59.4% work in the service sector but less than 0.6% are estimated to work in agriculture (the balance working in industry).<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="CARICOM_status_.26_The_CARICOM_Single_Market_Economy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="CARICOM_status_&amp;_The_CARICOM_Single_Market_Economy">CARICOM status &amp; The CARICOM Single Market Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: CARICOM status &amp; The CARICOM Single Market Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to the membership section of the CARICOM Community site, as of July 2, 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The British Virgin Islands holds Associate Member<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> status in CARICOM.
</p><p>In recognition of the CARICOM (Free Movement) Skilled Persons Act which came into effect in July 1997 in some of the CARICOM countries such as Jamaica and which has been adopted in other CARICOM countries,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> such as Trinidad and Tobago,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> it is possible that CARICOM nationals who hold the "A Certificate of Recognition of Caribbean Community Skilled Person" may be allowed to work in the BVI under normal working conditions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Transport in the British Virgin Islands">Transport in the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tortola-airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tortola-airport.jpg/220px-Tortola-airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tortola-airport.jpg/330px-Tortola-airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tortola-airport.jpg/440px-Tortola-airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1333" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tortola-airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terrance B. Lettsome International Airport on Tortola</div></div></div>
<p>There are 113 kilometres (70&#160;mi) of roads. The main airport, <a href="/wiki/Terrance_B._Lettsome_International_Airport" title="Terrance B. Lettsome International Airport">Terrance B. Lettsome International Airport</a>, also known as Beef Island Airport, is located on Beef Island, which lies off the eastern tip of Tortola and is accessible by the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II_Bridge,_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Queen Elizabeth II Bridge, British Virgin Islands">Queen Elizabeth II Bridge</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/LIAT" title="LIAT">LIAT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_Sunshine" title="Air Sunshine">Air Sunshine</a> are among the airlines offering scheduled service.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda_Airport" title="Virgin Gorda Airport">Virgin Gorda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auguste_George_Airport" title="Auguste George Airport">Anegada</a> have their own smaller airports. Private air charter services operated by <a href="/wiki/Island_Birds" title="Island Birds">Island Birds</a> Air Charter fly directly to all three islands from any major airport in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Helicopters are used to get to islands with no runway facilities; Antilles Helicopter Services is the only helicopter service based in the country.
</p><p>The main harbour is in <a href="/wiki/Road_Town" title="Road Town">Road Town</a>. There are also ferries that operate within the British Virgin Islands and to the neighbouring United States Virgin Islands. As in the UK and in the United States Virgin Islands, cars in the British Virgin Islands <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic#Jurisdictions_with_left-hand_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">drive on the left</a>; however, nearly all cars are <a href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Left hand drive">left hand drive</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> being imported from the United States. The roads are often quite steep, narrow and winding, and ruts can be a problem when it rains.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Demographics of the British Virgin Islands">Demographics of the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>As of the 2010 Census, the population of the territory was 28,054.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Current estimates put the population at 35,800 (July 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The majority of the population (83%) are <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="extiw" title="wikt:Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a>, descended from slaves brought to the islands by the British.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Other large ethnic groups include Latinos (5.5%), those of European ancestry (5.4%), native Amerindian (2.1%) and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> (1.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2004 Census reports:
</p>
<ul><li>83.4% <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">African</a></li>
<li>7% European/Caucasian</li>
<li>9.6% Others*</li></ul>
<p><span style="font-size:90%;">* Includes <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Caribbean">Indian</a>, Carib/Amerindian, Black/Carib mixed, and mixed-race Hispanic</span>
</p><p>The 2010 Census reports the main places of origin of residents as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>37% local born (though note that many locals go to St. Thomas or the United States for maternity services)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>7.2% Guyana</li>
<li>7.0% St. Vincent and the Grenadines</li>
<li>6.0% Jamaica</li>
<li>5.5% United States</li>
<li>5.4% Dominican Republic</li>
<li>5.3% United States Virgin Islands</li></ul>
<p><span style="font-size:90%;">* Includes <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Caribbean">Indian</a>, Carib/Amerindian, Black/Carib mixed, and mixed-race Hispanic.</span>
</p><p>The islands are heavily dependent upon migrant labour. In 2004, migrant workers accounted for 50% of the total population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 32% of workers employed in the British Virgin Islands work for the government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Unusually, the territory has one of the highest drowning mortality rates in the world, being higher than other high risk countries such as China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> 20% of deaths in the British Virgin Islands during 2012 were recorded as drownings,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> all of them being tourists. Despite this, the territory's most popular beach still has no lifeguard presence.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg/220px-Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg/330px-Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg/440px-Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jost_Van_Dyke_Methodist_Church_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jost Van Dyke Methodist Church</div></div></div>
<p>Over 90% of the population who indicated a religious affiliation at the 2010 Census were Christian<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> with the largest individual Christian denominations being <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> (17.6%),<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> (12%), <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Cleveland,_Tennessee)" title="Church of God (Cleveland, Tennessee)">Church of God</a> (11%) and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (9%).<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2001_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2001-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Constitution of the British Virgin Islands">Constitution of the British Virgin Islands</a> commences with a professed national belief in <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> constitute each approximately 1.2% of the population according to Word Religion Database 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_British_Virgin_Islands" title="Education in the British Virgin Islands">Education in the British Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The British Virgin Islands operates several government schools as well as private schools. There is also a community college, <a href="/wiki/H._Lavity_Stoutt_Community_College" title="H. Lavity Stoutt Community College">H. Lavity Stoutt Community College</a>, that is located on the eastern end of Tortola. This college was named after <a href="/wiki/Lavity_Stoutt" class="mw-redirect" title="Lavity Stoutt">Lavity Stoutt</a>, the first Chief Minister of the British Virgin Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> It is extremely common for students from the British Virgin Islands to travel overseas for tertiary education, either to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a>, or to colleges and universities in either the United Kingdom, United States or Canada.
</p><p>The literacy rate in the British Virgin Islands is high at 98%.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> Open campus in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Culture of the Virgin Islands">Culture of the Virgin Islands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Creole" title="Virgin Islands Creole">Virgin Islands Creole</a></div>
<p>The primary language is <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">British English</a>, although there is a local <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Creole" title="Virgin Islands Creole">dialect</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Spanish is spoken by <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Rican</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="People of the Dominican Republic">Dominican</a> and other Hispanic immigrants.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Music of the Virgin Islands">Music of the Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The traditional music of the British Virgin Islands is called <i>fungi</i> after the local <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">cornmeal</a> dish with the same name, often made with <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>. The special sound of fungi is due to a unique local fusion between African and European music. It functions as a medium of local history and folklore and is therefore a cherished cultural form of expression that is part of the curriculum in BVI schools.citation needed}} The fungi bands, also called "scratch bands", use instruments ranging from <a href="/wiki/Calabash" title="Calabash">calabash</a>, washboard, <a href="/wiki/Bongo_drum" title="Bongo drum">bongos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a>, to more traditional western instruments like keyboard, banjo, guitar, bass, triangle and saxophone. Apart from being a form of festive dance music, fungi often contains humorous social commentaries, as well as BVI oral history.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a></div>
<p>Because of its location and climate the British Virgin Islands has long been a haven for sailing enthusiasts. Sailing is regarded as one of the foremost sports in all of the BVI. Calm waters and steady breezes provide some of the best sailing conditions in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many sailing events are held in the waters of this country, the largest of which is a week-long series of races called the Spring Regatta, the premier sailing event of the Caribbean, with several races hosted each day. Boats include everything from full-size mono-hull yachts to dinghies. Captains and their crews come from all around the world to attend these races. The Spring Regatta is part race, part party, part festival. The Spring Regatta is normally held during the first week of April.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2009, the BVI have made a name for themselves as a host of international basketball events. The BVI hosted three of the last four events of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Basketball Championship">Caribbean Basketball Championship</a> (<i>FIBA CBC Championship</i>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Annual Report of the Civil Registry and Passport Office for 2012 which includes "For the 20 percent that represented drowning, all were tourists who died from snorkelling or diving in the VI waters in and around caves at <a href="/wiki/Norman_Island" title="Norman Island">Norman Island</a>, as well as near <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda" title="Virgin Gorda">Virgin Gorda</a>...The Virgin Islands should, therefore put safety measures in place such as the dissemination of information to hotels, dive shops and marinas." The same report confirms that the deaths of 86 persons were recorded in the Territory during 2012.</span>

<p><b><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Lat. <small>and</small> Long.</a> <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=British_Virgin_Islands&amp;params=18_25_53_N_64_37_23_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18°25′53″N</span> <span class="longitude">64°37′23″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.43139°N 64.62306°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.43139; -64.62306</span></span></span></a></span> <span style="color:darkblue;">(Road Town)</span></b>
